<Author>EmmaNigel
<Content>Lovely place to stay We stayed for three nights, and found this to be a clean, plush and comfortable hotel. We stayed in Room 512 which was on the top floor (in the roof), the room was just right for two people, not huge, but well arranged so we didn't feel 'squeezed' as you can feel so often in some places. It had a very decent bathroom with shower/bath and hairdyer, plus all the usual things and lotions (except soap, which came in a squeezy bottle on the wall). There is wifi, but you have to pay (10 euros for 24 hrs).We didn't have breakfast in the hotel (so can't comment), but it was extremely good to know that in the afternoon after walking around (freezing) Amsterdam, there was free coffee/hot choc/tea to warm you up whilst nibbling on the free pastries/biscuits whilst slumped in a comfy sofa reading the newspapers provided. There were no coffee making facilites in the room, and the minibar only contains water - but again, it is free.The staff were very friendly and helpful, and huge fish tank in reception was just awesome, my husband could barely tear himself away from it.

<Content>Mixed feelings If arriving by train, take a cab. It is really a long walk from the station unless you have no luggage and have 20-25 minutes to view things on the way. Arrived and was given a so so small room with no view. Asked for another. Hotel was accommodating to a point in that we were shown another bigger room or we could opt for a small room with a view. We opted for the broom closet sized room just for the view of the canal. (They claimed no others available. I was not so sure) This was our choice but two normal sized adults pretty much have to climb over each other to function.) Bathroom nice but very limited space on sink and shelf. View great from room . Bed was okay. No bed bugs that I could see or feel.(saw that in another review) Closet space....Poor. No drawers, a high hard to use shelf. (I lived better out of a foot locker in the Army). Beautifully decorated downstairs public rooms. Did not do the 16 Euro breakfast but room looked nice. Free coffee, cookies and candy in lobby area was nice touch . Bar open 24 hours. Fair prices on the drinks. Service was very good and staff helpful with a good restaurant recommendation. Price for 3 nights averages about 155 euros a night with taxes.

<Author>SWMatlock
<Content>Great little hotel The last couple of reviews don't compute with my own experience. I booked through a discount website and was therefore expecting one of the less good rooms. However on checking in I was given a room at the front of the hotel, overlooking the canal (207). The room was not huge (to be expected in Amsterdam) but was perfectly adequate and well designed (cubby holes to use as bedside storage). The bathroom was clean and much bigger than many I have experienced at far more expensive places. The staff were very polite and helpful and I found the facilities and location of the hotel to be very good (a 10 minute stroll from the central railway station). I made use of the free loan of a DVD player which was an added bonus.Downsides? None really, the wifi connection didn't work on the last day but I was refunded the cost of access with no question.

<Author>DonnaLJohnston
<Content>Nice Hotel Watch out for the Bed Bugs The hotel itself is very nice. However, watch out for the bedbugs. We stayed in room 406 at the hotel on the 24-26th October 2008, when my Husband and I woke up on the Saturday morning we noticed that we had little lumps on our skin but did not understand why. When we woke up Sunday morning with more bites I put 2+2 together. I woke up with a bite on my eye lid, which hurt and itched like hell. A week later I still have the lump without the redness!Since then, I have had to spray my home and my bags with the clothes I took to make sure this does not spread into my home. Once you have bedbugs they are hard to shift. Until now I did not know they actually existed. Its AWFUL! I have yet to email the hotel and see what repsonse I get, however, if you do stay here I would suggest you check the bed first before opening your luggage. Other than that, its a nice hotel and a nice location. I hope you have better luck than me!

<Author>Guinevere50
<Content>Unbelievable Breakfast! We stayed in Hotel Estherea for two nights this October. From the moment you enter its opulent panelled lobby you feel welcome. Our room wasn't quite ready and we were invited to help ourselves to free coffee, tea or hot chocolate (really good), while we waited. Our room overlooked the canal and had a pretty four poster bed. It boasted every convenience even down to the free slippers (well at least I hope they were free!). Breakfast was quite simply wonderful! Every conceivable thing you could possibly want to eat, from fresh fruit and smoothies, cereal, different breads and pastries to lovely crisply fried bacon, 'proper' sausages and eggs (scrambled or fried). Once we ate here in the morning, we didnt need anything until dinner time! We walked everywhere from this hotel, it couldn't be better placed for any attraction you may wish to visit. My only critiscism would be the lack of proper lighting to read by at night and to fix my face in the morning (!) and our bathroom was a little small, but these were minor flaws. I would recommend this hotel to anyone who wants to feel spoiled and relaxed at the end of a day.

Have you ever heard of such proactiveness?All in all - I arrived at the Hotel at 6pm and only hit my bed at 5am to check out at 10am the next day. I had a great stay in Amsterdam and this Hotel was a big part of the reason.

<Author>rachelmle
<Content>We loved it! Beautiful hotel, great staff, free goodies! We LOVED the Hotel Estherea. My husband and I stayed at the hotel for 4 nights and found it to be wonderful. It was in a great location - about a 5 minute walk to Dam Square and about 20 mins to the Anne Frank House and Central Station.The staff was always approachable and helpful. They booked tickets for us for the Anne Frank house, in order to skip over the very very long line. I highly suggest doing this. We got our tickets at the hotel front desk, and skipped an hour long line to walk straight into the museum. The tickets were the same price as buying them directly at the Anne Frank House. The staff also provided us with free ponchos and use of umbrellas during the rainy days.If coffee shops are on your agenda, there are many places near the hotel to check out. There are 2 shops within a 3-5 minute walk and dozens more within a 5-15 minute walk.The free cookies/pastries/coffee/tea/hot chocolate in the lobby was a great perk. We saved quite a few Euros by snacking at the hotel instead of at a cafe!Breakfast is 16 Euro per person, which is quite pricey. We peeked into the breakfast room one morning to see what we were missing and we were not missing much. We opted out of breakfast and went to a small bakery on the corner. We each ate breakfast for 5 Euro there - a much better choice than the 16 Euro option!We ate dinner one night at Caprese - the Italian restaurant on the street behind the hotel with the yellow and white awning. It was inexpensive, compared to many other restaurants in the area and it was absolutely delicious.Our room was wonderful. The bed was ok - not the best, but certainly not the worst. My only complaint in the room was the hair dryer. It was very weak and semi-broken. (I had to hold down the on button constantly or else the dryer would turn off.) Other than that, the room was great!I would certainly put this hotel in a 4 star class - not a 3 star, as listed. I have stayed in many 3, 4, and 5 star properties - and this is certainly a 4 star, considering all of its amenities.

<Content>An Ideal Hotel and Haven in Amsterdam We stayed at the Estherea as a birthday treat and stayed for 3 nights over a weekend. <Author>karlimd
<Content>Great Stay!!! Loved The Estherea! We stayed at The Hotel Estherea for 3 nights in June. What a great hotel....everything that has been said is true...great location,beautiful lobby,free tea /coffee/snacks. There were 4 of us, 2adults and our 2 children(ages 13  15). It is difficult in Europe to find either connecting rooms or rooms that will accommodate 4 people. At the Estherea we had a quad room. It was fine for the 4 of us. It faced the street behind the hotel (no canal view),but it was a lovely street view. We had a king bed and 2 doubles with plenty of room. The room also had a desk  chair, plus 2 sitting chairs, a flat screen TV,and a large closet. The bathroom was clean and stocked with nice products. The real beauty of this hotel was the staff....very,very nice,great advice and restaurant recommendations. We had drinks at the bar which was nice, but never had breakfast at the hotel. If you walk out of the hotel, turn left and make a quick left at the side street, on the right side there is a great bakery (3 minute walk)...we got fresh treats in the morning and had them in our room with coffee. The breakfast price at the hotel was a little steep at 16E per person. Be sure and take Mike's Bike Tour while in Amsterdam...it was one of the highlights of our trip!! If you have any questions let me know!! Happy travels!

<Author>Hosalito
<Content>Charming Respite in the Heart of a Great City We stayed at the Estherea for 3 nights at the end of our honeymoon. I am so glad TripAdvisor is available, as I would never have found this gem otherwise. The hotel is tucked into the quiet Singel Canal, in a great part of town. Our room was #210 and looked out over the Singel. The street itself is very quiet, and while it's only 1 or 2 blocks from all of the action, we could never tell while we were in the room! All we could hear out of the windows is the everyday hustle and bustle of Amsterdam (think bike bells!). Our room had a double bed and a sitting area with a desk, plus of course a nicely appointed bathroom. The products in the bathroom were wonderful and the towels were very lush!There is an area in the lobby where they serve free coffee, tea, candy and cakes all day and night. Plus, fresh fruit! There is also a bar area that is fully stocked, so you can get a drink at any time, plus they have the most wonderful mint-flavored water available (that's free!).There is an elevator but you can also take the stairs if you are so inclined. If you exit the hotel and turn left, there is a Greek deli/restaurant that serves up AMAZING, authentic dishes. It's great for a quick bite! Lastly, I cannot say enough about the staff. In true Dutch fashion, they were patient, gracious, and willing to help with any request....all with a smile!

<Author>GoGirlToo
<Content>Absolutely Wonderful Hotel We stayed over in Amsterdam for four nights en route to Prague -- my mother, my sister  I. We all had a fabulous time at the Hotel Estherea -- and agreed it was one of the nicest places ever. The hotel is in a perfect location on a quiet  lovely canal within easy walking distance of many major sites (Dam Square/Anne Frank House); a tram stop is just a block or so behind the hotel. There are many excellent  reasonably priced restaurants very close by. The staff couldn't have been nicer or more helpful and made excellent suggestions for restaurants, tours, etc.. Best of all, the hotel is gorgeously decorated in old-fashioned Dutch style. It's a very atmospheric canal house, but with all of the modern comforts -- and then some. Coffee, a large assortment of teas, cocoa or ice water (with mint  lemon) are always available for guests to enjoy; in the afternoons  at night savories and/or sweets (e.g. gingerbread, pastries, olives etc.) are also set out. As Amsterdam was still cold in early April (though the hotel was always warm), we got into the habit of enjoying tea in the afternoon  camomile tea with cake at night while watching the interesting tropical fish tank in the beautiful livingroom/lobby before heading up to bed. Our room for 3 was large and very beautiful; the bathroom was large and well-equiped. All and all, a wonderful treat. I''d love to go back -- anytime!!  
<Date>May 14, 2008

<Author>Wanderer151
<Content>Tiny Shabby Room I have been to Amsterdam a dozen times in the last 10 years and stayed at a different hotel each time because I've never had a good hotel experience in Amsterdam: tiny rooms and tinier bathrooms, high prices and staff that range from cooly efficient to condescending insolence. So when I read the glowing reviews of the Estherea, I had hope - unfortunately unfounded. I was assigned the smallest room in the hotel although my rate was the normal one for a double room (well over $300US/night). It was so small, that when I took the large decorative pillows off the bed the only place to put them was on the floor and that left maybe 5 narrow feet to walk around the bed that was wedged in an alcove. The room could best be described as shabby, carpet that hadn't been changed in 20 years (an issue because you had to get on your hands and knees to get to the room safe in the bottom of the cupboard - not a closet). There were holes in the walls left unfilled, 80's style metallic wall paper and beat up cheaply made furniture. It did have a view on the canal, but that just meant it was noisy - I could hear a couple talking at normal voice through the walls too. I asked to move and of course they were full. The staff was reasonably friendly but not helpful. The only good points were the neighborhood and the breakfast. The lobby was rather grand, but in the flower capital of the world it was odd to see so many fake, glittery flower arrangements and I never spent time in the lobby anyway. So still searching for a decent reasonably priced hotel in Amsterdam.

<Author>ohmyGOSH
<Content>Wonderful experience I was delighted with this hotel which I booked after reading the very favorable comments on TA. I travel to Amsterdam monthly for business. This Spring I decided to take a few days for touring with my daughter and was looking for a less expensive option than the business class hotel I where I usually stay. We`loved the Estherea - even though we ended up with a small room on the interior. The hotel is so well located, slightly to west of the center of old town, so we spent most of our time touring the city and didn't mind the room. The beds were fine, the bathroom small but clean and modern. The lobby and room are charmingly european. There is always drinks and sweets available for guest. The staff was polite and helpful. I am sure we will stay here again.The location of the hotel is great. Unless you are into the honkey tonk bar scene, sex workers, or just general touristy places, I highly recommend the quieter west side of the historic downtown. The streets and canals are elegant, it feels very safe, and you won't be awaken by the rowdy bar crawlers in the middle of the night. There are also very affordable cafes in the area, with very good and healthy food. We enjoyed being the only Americans eating in these establishments!

<Author>Langton_Traveller
<Content>Bloomin' great We have just returned from a 3 night city break with our 2 children and were delighted with our hotel choice. We used the fast  efficient train service between the airport and central station. The hotel is a 15/20 minute stroll, if it's not raining, and its central location means that pretty much everything is within walking distance - although the trams are easy to use when legs get weary.The room (419) was ready for us on arrival at 1.00pm and there was plenty of space for all 4 of us - no canal view, but the windows open onto the interesting cityscape. Our bed was large  comfy, and the large sleigh-like sofa converted into 2 single beds. The bathroom was small but adequate. We found the staff friendly and helpful and the whole hotel felt spotlessly clean  well maintained/decorated.The breakfasts offered plenty of choice, including hot (bacon, sausages  eggs) and cost 14 euros per person (children under 11 free). However, there are plenty of cafes nearby - a couple of good ones 5 mins walk looking out onto the flower market - and offer much cheaper alternatives.There is plenty of choice for restaurants in the evening. The hotel recommended the Haesje Claes just around the corner, where we enjoyed the typically-Dutch, and very filling, food. There was a childrens menu and prices were reasonable.All-in-all, the Estherea is a great base from which to enjoy this fascinating city.

<Author>MaryJane03
<Content>An excellent hotel,  We are just back from 4 nights at the Hotel Estherea. It is an outstanding hotel. It is beautifully decorated and extremely well run. The hotel staff is very helpful. Some of them might be a little formal, but all tried their best to help us in any way they could, from getting dining reservations to having a room for us when we arrived at 7 am - amazing! The location was unbeatable - no matter where we wanted to go in the city, it was an easy walk. We finally took the tram the last night, just for the experience. We had a double without the canal view, but it was very spacious. The bathroom, though small, was both spotless, and well equipped. The price was very fair. Even with the sad state of the dollar, it average the same as a recent stay at the San Diego Embassy Suites. I can't thank all the reviewers enough for all the great information that they have given in their reviews. They helped make our trip go smoothly. From needing our credit card pin number to get the train tickets from the airport to finding the Gollum - a neat brown cafe -your advice was invaluable. I strongly recommend reading all the reviews you can- I felt so comfortable choosing restaurants and finding places - like the advice from about 25 close friends!Don't hesitate trying the Luden - just around the block. The food was terrific, reasonably priced, especially in the Brasserie in the front,and felt like being in Paris. The Cafe Luxembourg was also fun, and just a little further down the street. The soups and fries were especially good. The hotel's location near so many great restaurants is just icing on the cake. We tried the hotel breakfast, and it was very good, but also crowded because they were full while we were there. So we only ate there once. Broodje Bert on the corner serves a bargain full breakfast or just a roll if you want, simple but fun to sit down and watch the world go by in front of you while sipping your coffee.Yes, we had a wonderful time. The weather was cold and rainy - it even snowed. But it didn't matter, we had such a good time in Amsterdam - we recommend it highly- and everyone spoke English!

<Author>SISTERACT4
<Content>A Real Gem I am just back from the Hotel Estherea having spent 4 nights there with my 3 sisters. We booked a quadruple room (yes we are a close family!) which was quite spacious compared to the cramped offering of Paris the previous year. The hotel is located on the Singel canal which is a quiet part of the city but also very central for site seeing. The hotel has a quaint olde worlde feel to it the moment you enter. Luxurious fabrics, carpets and curtains are used throughout the hotel as well as 2 very spectacular chandeliers in the lobby - quality and class without being stuffy. There is a fantastic aquarium just inside the front door which we spent 10 minutes looking at everytime we left or returned to the hotel! Beakfast was a buffet style and of a very high standard with plenty of variety to cater for all tastes. The other nice touch was the complimentary hot drinks, chocolates, fruit, sweets and cakes which were available throughout the day and of course the resident housecat that occasionally graced the lobby! The staff were also very helpful and courteous. For beer lovers there is a cafe down the side street from the hotel - Cafe Gollem which sells over 200 speciality beers.

<Author>bertrande80
<Content>Great location, ambience No hotel booking website had this hotel available for our required dates so we had to book this straight from the hotel, which was fine.We arrived in Amsterdam very early on 1 March and arrived at the hotel at 7am. We were efficiently checked in but the room was not ready so we hung around before the weather became more conducive for outdoor exploration. We really liked the cosy intimate decoration downstairs, which wasn't too ornate but which had an air of old elegance and detail. The library was well stocked and the chairs were very comfortable.The room we had (#316) had no view but was more than sufficient for 2 persons. Amenities were as expected, although we did find the bed (queen-sized) a little small because we were so used to our king-sized bed at home. Room was well furnished and decorated and I didn't find the internet rate of 10 euros a day (from 12pm to 12pm the next day) exorbitant.Reception was always courteous and polite and the breakfast spread was simple yet good (14 euros per person), with a small but fresh selection of hams, cheeses, fruits and some hot dishes.Location was great for walking everywhere (we only ever took the tram once in our entire 3-night stay), except when we were lugging our luggage from the central station to the hotel. I would definitely recommend this as a good alternative to the numerous large chain hotels in the city.

<Author>ambercostley
<Content>Decent hotel with a few bad experiences My husband and I stayed here from October 8th-14th, in a canal room, which I requested ahead of time when I booked through their website. Our room was fairly large and the view of the canal out of the front windows was fantastic. The lobby was beautiful, breakfast was pretty good, and there were lots of nice spots to hang out and have tea or coffee in. The location was terrific, pretty central to things that we wanted to do and only a few blocks away from a train. The staff was perfectly fine, they helped us when we needed help and were always polite.The room did have a few bad points however, and I was fairly disappointed after reading all of the excellent reviews on Trip Advisor. While the room did look fairly nice, the bed was horrible and had both me and my husband tossing and turning. He actually lost a fair amount of sleep one night because he was just so uncomfortable. We got a bit used to it after a couple of nights and to be fair we are a bit pampered by our mattress at home, but this was just awful. I've slept on fold out sofa beds that were more comfortable.Then there was the bathroom. I have stayed in many hotels with teeny bathrooms, that wasn't the problem. The problem was the mildew, stained towels, and bad ventilation. I can honestly say this was the worst hotel bathroom I have ever been in. Just very unpleasant overall. One thing that we did not have a problem with was the squeaky floorboards. The noise from other rooms and floors seemed fairly minimal to me, but we live in a flat that is on the second floor of a three floor hundred year old building with wood flooring on each level, so both floor noise and hearing other people is probably less likely to get to me then other people. Overall a very pretty hotel, and we had a decent stay there, but the bed and bathroom will keep us from returning.

<Author>GoldTraveller

<Author>Rangnath
<Content>Luxury and Indolence We have just returned from a 3 night stay at the Estherea. The hotel is excellent with really good service. We were just expecting a few bits but breakfast is a lovely Dutch/continental spread and the restaurants, for an evening meal, are all round the hotel and are of great value with good food. This hotel is one of the most convenient for restaurants, coffee shops and bars. We found a Bar that allows cigar/cigarette smoking and drinking and, although neither of us smoke tobacco, we enjoyed the 'old' style of Dutch Bar and if you want to mix a little luxury with the odd trip shopping then this is an absolute must as it's just round the corner from ALL the shops on the Damrak.The staff at the hotel seem to go by the maxim of, 'we can do it and if we can't then we know someone who can'.This is a 'Family Run Hotel' and family owned in every meaning of the word and it really does feel like home once you get into your room after a day wandering and shopping.Overall I would say this is probably the best hotel we have ever stayed at in Amsterdam on holiday.

<Author>JLM_7
<Content>You can't smoke cannabis here ! We stayed at the Estheria for the first time and would advise anyone who wants a cozy, friendly, and smoke free enviornment to give it a try. I heard people complain about paying $15.00 for breakfast but the complementry hot drinks, cakes, biscuits and fruit available in their fantastic lobby/bar 24 hours a day more more than compensate for this. The Estheria has an in house rule that bans the smoking of any cannabis products ANYWHERE in the hotel. They will add $150 to your bill should they catch you, and they WILL catch you! They have very few smoking rooms(tobacco only) so make sure you make it clear when you book if you need a smoking room. A great hotel for non smokers. If you smoke but dont have a smoking room you will have to smoke on the street! We will be returning in 2008.

<Author>AnaMo
<Content>What a great hotel....! This hotel was one of those rare things...a perfect fit. Not a big chain so it had a personal touch, but very well appointed. The location was excellent in one of the inner canal rings on Singel. There was great dining and shopping nearby. We stayed at a chain hotel for one night before Estherea and it was more expensive and much less pleasant. Our Estherea room was just configured great, the bathroom had 2 sinks, plenty of room and a great shower (the actual bath faucet has to be turned the the left to get the shower to work-it was a bit tricky). The rooms were updated with great linens and very clean. The common areas were very cozy. I didn't eat at the hotel restaurant. Breakfast is very pricey and we didn't want to eat that much so we went a few doors down to get a baguette for breakfast-1 Euro. One thing I loved about the hotel was the free coffee/tee bar they have in the lobby. It's a beautiful bit of custom-built carpenty that has all sorts of teas, sweeteners, and an awesome coffee maker where you just press a button. This is a great perk in a hotel when you just want to get going in the morning and don't want to have to sit down and order a simple cup of coffee. We couldn't stop saying how great we thought the hotel was. We paid a bit more for a canal view (our room was 314 and great) but it really made our stay nicer being able to look out onto the canal. I totally recommend this.

<Content>A wonderful hotel I loved this hotel from the moment we drove up to the front door. We were met by Rudy, who was wonderful and took care of us very well. We arrived early, at 10am. The aquarium in the hotel is also amazing.The hotel is in a quiet and central location, within walking distance of many of the sights. Good restaurants can be found in the street behind the hotel, and lots of shops in the pedestrian street behind that. We did not have breakfast at the hotel. There is a great place on the corner called Bertje, or something similar. They do a good breakfast for 7 euros.

<Author>carolandbob
<Content>Beautiful decor, lovely breakfast and fantastic location!! As a trip leader for a NJ Ski Club, I brought a group of 46 to the Hotel Estherea for 3 nights after a week of skiing in Italy in March.Everyone was so impressed with the hotel and its staff, that my husband and I returned the first weekend in Sept. with 6 friends before embarking on a cruise. The rooms are clean and well appointed. Although the rooms that faced the street to the rear of the hotel had larger double-sink marble bathrooms , we again opted for the front rooms with 4 canal facing windowsfor a wonderful view. Ask for Rooms 110, 112, 210 or 212. for a canal view. For a city with pricey hotels, we were happy to pay 185 euro per night to stay in such an elegant small hotel. It is quite comfortable to sit in the lobby or read a newspaper in the library while enjoying a complimentary cup of coffee, tea or hot chocolate and cookies. There is also a small staffed bar.The buffet breakfast was included in the price and was nicely done. It included eggs, sausages, cold cuts and cheeses, cereals, fresh fruits and juices, and marvelous assortment of homebaked breads and pastries.It's location on Singel makes it a short walk to all the attractions and around the corner from the excellent classic Dutch restaurant, Haesje Claes.

<Author>m0thily
<Content>You probably can't go wrong here. This hotel is a welcome respite in a city of questionable lodgings. The decor is classy and warm, and it has an old charm that for once *doesn't* mean run-down and cramped.The room we stayed in (four nights) was small. Not quite Manhattan small, but definitely not spacious. Enough room for two people and two suitcases. The bed was comfortable and large, and the hotel staff was more than willing to give us extra pillows. We had a view of some other rooms' windows (very close by), so we had to keep the curtains closed at all times. If possible, I'd recommend asking for a room with an exterior view.The bathroom was clean and luxurious. My only gripe with the bathroom was that the towels were a bit too small. Chalk that up to Americans wanting everything to be oversized!The breakfast buffet here is pretty decent... I think we paid 14 euros per person, and we got fruit, cereal, scrambled eggs, pastries, etc. Standard, but fresh and well-stocked. They gave us free (small) bottles of water in the guest room every day, which is a nice touch.Unfortunately, I think our guest room was right above the kitchen area, so every morning around 7am, we heard the swinging doors to the kitchen and the clanging of plates right through the vents in our room. It wasn't a huge deal, and might not be an issue in other rooms, but you might want to bring earplugs just in case, if you plan on sleeping past 7am.Another minor gripe is the hotel's strange policy of wanting you to leave your room key at the front desk when you leave. The keys are on a keyring that has a magnificently posh tassle on it... which would be cumbersome to carry around, anyway. But this means that you have to wait in line at the front desk to get your key or drop off your key. In other words, allow yourself a few minutes on the way back to your guest room. ...I'm reluctant to mention it here, but you have to wonder how easy it would be for a thief to get into a guest room by simply asking the staff for a certain guest room's key by number. They didn't check our ID or anything when we asked for our key.In all, we'd recommend this hotel to anyone staying in Amsterdam. The neighborhood is quiet but close to everything (we're big walkers and were able to walk everywhere). You probably can't go wrong with this hotel in terms of comfort and value.  
<Date>Sep 6, 2007

<Author>iblaurajc
<Content>Favorite hotel of our two week Europe trip This was our first and favorite hotel of a two week Europe vacation (we stayed in 6 hotels). The Estherea is sparkling clean, rooms of acceptable size. Charming boutique hotel with a gorgeous, welcoming, cozy lobby with separate sitting rooms. Fresh orchids everywhere. Free coffee (mediocre), tea and hot chocolate at all hours, often with snacks as well. GREAT quiet location on Singel canal a couple blocks from Dam Square. Staff seemed competent , if not particularly warm (although I will single out one guy, Igor, who worked hard to get us reservations for the Anne Frank house when there was a problem with the internet site). By the way, you must have reservations to Anne Frank; we went at 7:30 pm and there was still a line around the block. We didnt' have problems getting into any other museums. Only downside was the charge for internet - 5 euros for a half hour. All other hotels during our European stay offered free internet use. We would definitely stay here again and look no further. Another nice touch- refrigerator in room stocked with two free bottles of water each day of our 3 night stay. We absolutely loved this hotel. Felt great to return here each night.

<Author>Lifeonholiday
<Content>Elegance and Privacy The Estherea is a beautiful hotel on the Singel Canal. The interior is done in highly romantic style, with amazing flower arrrangements everywhere. Everything is clean and well-maintained. The staff are helpful and unflaggingly friendly, and since they ask you to leave your key at the desk, you are always welcomed home personally. I had a wonderful room with a canal view and while it could get somewhat noisy from time to time - I was there on Gay Pride weekend, so it's hard to tell what's normal - if I closed the drapes and shut the windows at night, I slept like a baby.The very best part about the Hotel is that it is perfectly within walking distance of every major attraction and enough off the beaten track that, when you come back to the Hotel, all the hustle and bustle of the tourist areas disappears.At the nearest corner is a small cafe that has the freshest salads in Amsterdam. I would skip the breakfast at the hotel and eat at this cafe or walk to the flower market - five minutes away - and have a classic Dutch pancake and watch the world go by.This hotel is a jewel. I plan to stay here again.

<Author>RWCFamily
<Content>Need to be a heavy sleeper I picked this hotel for the first two nights of our trip to Europe with our toddler. I knew it was a little out of the way and wanted to make sure we were in a quiet location to get our sleep. I was pleasently suprised when we got there. Finally, my husband took my (now crying) daugher to the lobby and the front desk clerk handed him the keys to the suite on the top floor. Otherwise, you better be a good sleeper.I regret to say that I had read other complaints about noise in this hotel before making my reservation.

<Author>MahrtianWanderer
<Content>Estherea Lives Up to its Fine Reputation We had elevated expectations about the Estherea, given the positive reviews, and we are happy to report that this small hotel is indeed a great find. Our room was very comfortable, recently renovated and decorated with superb taste and a sense of style. The beds were deep and comfy; the chairs and other furniture luxurious, in an old world way. It had a large bath with a double sink, which I did not expect. The public areas on the ground floor are especially inviting, for a coffee and a sweet treat, or a drink in the evening. These rooms have fabulous wood paneling, particularly in the stunning library. Everything was very well maintained and in perfect working order.The unexpected bonus about the Estherea is that it is in a great location, on the innermost canal known as Singel. The back of the hotel looks over Spuistraat, which has an abundance of the city's best restaurants, cafes and bookstores. We had all of our dinners (four nights) at restaurants that were within a block of the hotel - Haseje Claes, Kantjil and Tigre, and the Luden. All very different and all highly recommended. The Greek deli next door and the bakery down the alley on Spuistraat are also outstanding. You can tell we did our fair share of eating while in Amsterdam.From the Estherea, we could walk 15 minutes and be at the Rijksmuseum, the van Gogh, or the Concertgebouw. Or, one can take the street trolley, which is also just a block from the hotel. And, for the sheer pleasure of it, just wandering around the neighborhood, seeing the magnificent buildings on those delightful canals, peeking into stores and brasseries, bakeries and boutiques, taking in what makes Amsterdam so special, is the best reason to stay at the Estherea.  
<Date>Jul 31, 2007

<Author>PhilosParis
<Content>Disappointing - why is it so highly rated This hotel is highly rated and we cannot understand why when you have so much choice in Amsterdam for others.They first proposed room 405 (standard room) which is a very tiny room with no view (there are others like this one actually). You can actually find better in an economy hotel for far less money. We refused the room (they were maybe expecting we would accept it because we booked it on the internet with a discount - why do they have to try it, thinking people are stupid - it is always unpleasant to refuse rooms). We changed to room 415. This room was a little bit bigger, still with no view and had really nothing special. We had to accept it as we were told there was nothing else. We waked up several times during the two nights of our stay. We could actually hear each step of the neighbors on top (what is unpleasant) and more important the hotel was noisy (you can easely hear the neighbors when they come during the night, when they leave in the morning or when they just talk). On top of that, the shower was not working the second day.Globally, we found this hotel very expensive for what it is (especially if you have to pay 250 euros for a standard - basic room) and were disappointed. Of course, the location is good and the bibliotheque charming but this is not obviously where people sleep and rest to better enjoy the city later on.

<Author>leavingNJ
<Content>My New Favorite City and Hotel From the first second we arrived, my mother and I, the staff was very warm and friendly. They let us see many options for our room before we chose the one we stayed in. The rooms were very well kept with a very fancy decor. The rooms had a refridgerator, safe, hairdryer, ac, heat, and a tv. The hotel had an elevator which helps with carrying luggage up the narrow and steep houses of amsterdam. The front desk was so helpful with arranging dinner or attraction reservations. The last thing that I found very impressive was that the hallway by the restaurant, had coffee, hot chocolate, hot water for tea and at many times of the day, they had fresh fruits and pastries. The hotel location is fantastic. Just two blocks from Dam square, but yet the hotel is situated in a quieter area. The hotel is also near the tram stops in front of the palace. I would recommend that you see, the Anne Frank house, Rijksmuseum, Van Gogh Museum, and take a bike tour or walking tour of the city to see all the historic sights. Parting notes: Take a canal tour, ride bikes through the city, and visit the historic quater and the red light district. Have fun!

<Author>supremecourt25
<Content>Can't say one bad thing about this hotel!! Amazing!! This hotel hands-down deserves the Traveler's Choice award (very proudly displayed on their front counter - so cute!). I requested room 417 because I had read it had a really nice canal view. I kind of badgered the hotel about it before arriving, which apparently worked because I got room 317, which also had a nice view. They knew exactly my preferences when I checked in! Nice size room, gorgeous linens, although the bathroom towels were itty-bitty! Very odd. Great bath products and the shower had a retractable clothesline, which was really cool and which we utilized. I paid 220 per night for the room which did NOT include tax - so it was more like 230 per night. Well worth it though - it was close enough to be within walking distance of everything we wanted to see, yet far enough from the RLD to be away from the noise and riffraff. Excellent. Everyone who worked the front desk was really friendly and nice - another place where you have to turn in and recieve your key whenever you leave or come back - sigh! The one exception was one lady who personally struck me as weird and not helpful. I don't recall her name, but she was in her late 40s or so, had blond hair and glasses and was short. She gave us a weird fake smile whenever we saw her and we ended up avoiding her whenever possible. When we first arrived, I asked for a recommendation for a good Thai restaurant within walking distance and she got this puzzled look on her face like she had never been asked that question in her life! she immediately went over to the computer, presumably to do a google search. Amsterdam has a gazillion good Thai restaurants, according to my guidebooks and friends who have visited there - not a weird question by any means! When I saw her going to the computer for help I said forget it, please just recommend anyplace good within walking distance. She recommended Broodje Bert, right next to the hotel. Although the food wasn't horrible, I can't recommend this place. They are just sandwiches and the service is excruciatingly slow, even by European standards. I would have walked a little further, had I known how close the pancake restaurants were to the hotel. One really nice gentleman working the front desk recommended an Indian restaurant, Shiva, which was awesome. The free coffee and water were also a nice touch. The afternoon snacks were a nice idea, but imo didn't taste very good.My only real complaint was that when I made the reservation, the hotel emailed me that the rate did not include tax or breakfast. But one day out of desperation, we decided to eat the breakfast even though it was 14 Euros per day. The buffet was excellent and no complaints - except that everyone there seemed to have the breakfast included in their rate. Nobody asked us for our room number or had us sign anything - we could have been eating the breakfast all three days!! Why tell me that it wasn't included? I felt kind of ripped off in that regard. Overall I would stay here again without hesitation. I feel certain that this is the nicest hotel of its class in Amsterdam. Request a room facing the canal and you will be in heaven!  
<Date>Jun 21, 2007

<Author>MissContented
<Content>Fantastic I have just returned from a break with my husband in Amsterdam from 29th May to 1st June and had a fabulous time at Hotel Estherea.I found the Hotel at the last minute going through the internet and booked direct with the hotel. Absolutely gorgeous hotel which is located down Singel Road right by a canal which was quiet and only a 5 minute walk to Dam Square. Room was a bit small but very tastefully decorated and enough space for what you needed. We also asked for a canal view room when we arrived and were not charged any extra for it. Hotel Staff were really friendly and helpful, nothing too much trouble. Tea, coffee etc all complimentary 24 hours a day in the reception area, help yourself. Nothing in rooms but okay to go downstairs and take up to the room. Cake and fruit also complimentary. Did not have breakfast in hotel as not up early enough! We got a train from the airport for 4 euros each and it was only a 15/20 minute journey. Much cheaper than taxi and then we walked to the hotel from station.Recommend Majestic Bar in Dam Square for a drink and spot of people watching! It served Thai food and nibbles as well which was reasonably priced and tasty. Also Caressa Restaurant (I think) little Italian behind the hotel which was really good. Very busy so a good sign to eat there. Bar De Waag in New Square Market really good for midday snacks and evening meal.Definitely recommend to my friends and would definitely go back again.One thing I would suggest is that we went from Tuesday to Friday so missed the majority of the stag/hen parties. As we sat in Dam Square on the Friday afternoon they were all turning up in their job lot t-shirts so if you wanted a romantic break without the rowdy parties then go midweek!!

<Author>Dotty8
<Content>Perfect location We are a group of 11ladies and have just returned from a weekend in Amsterdam. We chose the Hotel Estherea by the excellent reviews and were not disappointed. The hotel is beautiful and the tea, coffee, hot chocolate and cookies available 24hrs in the lobby was a real bonus. The location is excellent, very quiet picturesque canalside location but only a few minutes easy walking to the centre. We checked in late due to flights (hotel was advised) and the staff were very helpful as they were throughout our stay. The Concierge recommended a Dutch restaurant for Saturday night that was just around the corner from the hotel and this too was very good, excellent food and good value. Initially we were disappointed that we were not given the canal side view that we asked for, instead we had rooms facing a tiny courtyard - but this wasn't a problem as it was very quiet. Amsterdam is a lovely city, definately recommend the Canal bus tours especially for a short stay as you can see most of the city and it is very informative. Should we go back I will definately stay at the Estherea and recommend others to do so as well.

<Author>MissusM
<Content>Very Nice Stay -- Would certainly stay again We had a very pleasant 8 day stay in April, myself and my two sons. Their father joined us after several days, though we were given the Family room at the start, though at a reduction until we were indeed reunited as a family (of 4). The hotel is very conveniently located within the central ring of Amerstdam, on the Singel canal, and within easy walking distance to Dam Square Central Station. Day trips were therefore made very easy, and the hotel provided info if one preferred guided tours of the city and countryside. There are many very good restaurants right behind the hotel on the Spui and very conveniently located groceries (the ubiquitous ah:) and department stores within blocks. The hotel itself is run by very coureous and pleasant staff, is comfortably and elegant furnished, and offers a complimentry afternoon tea. Breakfast was good, though at14 Euros not a terrific value (though our 12 and 7 year old ate for free, which offset the expense). Had our room only been a bit bigger, things would have been ideal, but they were very fine, indeed, and we'd gladly repeat the experience.

<Author>swanseabayview
<Content>Beautiful Estherea 11th April 2007We booked the Estherea through Hotels.nl. and loved our stay from 3rdto 6th April. From Schiphol airport we got the train from under the airport to Central Station. This was rather confusing for novices - you need to ensure you have enough coins to buy tickets from the machines - 3 Euro 60 each, or pay more at the ticket office. The hotel is almost a mile from there, so we got tram 5 to Spuistraat, from where the hotel was just a short walk. We were lucky to get a large room and bathroom on the top floor, but no view as it looked into the internal courtyard/lightwell. I was disappointed at first because of this, but it turned out not to be a problem as we spent very little time in the room. The room was very well furnished and decorated to a high standard. Everything was immaculately clean. Igor would have changed our room if we'd wanted to, but I soon got to like it. The staff are very friendly, helpful and polite. The ground floor of the hotel has sumptuous, classically elegant decor, which I loved, and we spent quite a bit of time relaxing and enjoyingthis area. The chandeliers are something else. They have put in a lotof thought here to cater well for guests, with a wide selection of complimentary beverages, in Delft china, on tap constantly in the foyer. Fruit, chocolates, pastries and cookies were also offered. All this can be enjoyed in the comfortable lounges/library/bar - somewhere to relax and enjoy meeting other guests. We enjoyed meeting some American guests - it is a sociable hotel because of these common areas. The tropical fish tank in the lounge area is fabulous - it has an awesome variety of fish, and various beautiful corals growing in it.The hotel is well located on the Singel Canal, a quietish (not much traffic - mainly bikes) upmarket area, where you are spoilt for choice for bars, cafes, restaurants and pastry shops within easy walking distance. Spuistraat, behind the hotel, has lots of restaurants and ends in Spui Square, which buzzes with cafes and bars. We enjoyed Cafe Luxembourg here. We also enjoyed dutch food at Haesje Claes on Spuistraat, Italian at Casa di David on Singel - lovely ambience, and Indonesian at Cilubang on Runstraat (we had the Reijstaffel, an interesting selection of small dishes rather like tapas). Broodje Bert, next block down, is good for very reasonably priced lunch. (Bertburger was excellent)!We had lots of rides on the Canal Bus - a fun way to get a good look around the city. We didn't use the trams because you can easily walk to most places from Singel You have to be very 'bike aware' as they are everywhere! I will hire one next time to save my feet from aching at night after so much walking on cobbles. I am already planning to return in the Autumn and would choose to stay at the Estherea again. Thanks to the staff for a super holiday. Sue and Richard (The Welsh folks from Swansea).  
<Date>Apr 11, 2007

<Author>loobyloos
<Content>Lovelely hotel We stayed at the hotel Estherea for three nights, 18th to 21st March and were given a lovely room on the fifth floor overlooking the street and city. It was absolutely spotless, spacious and very well decorated with a great bathroom.The public areas also were immaculate, cosy and very comfortable - it was a pleasure to come back to the hotel after a day sightseeing, especially as it was very cold while we were there - it snowed one morning! Coffee, tea etc. are available free of charge in the lobby and there is also a lovely little bar and a library.The hotel is in a perfect location to explore the city on foot. Public transport is plentiful and there is a tram stop two streets behind the hotel which we caught to get to Central Station and from there took a train back to the airport on our return home.. We also took a canal bus; tickets can be bought at reception and last all day and until noon the next day.Igor and the rest of the reception staff were all extremely friendly and helpful which made our stay all the better.There are numerous restaurants in the area, we especially liked the Haesje Claes on the road behind the hotel, which was very handy.All in all we had a great trip and will definately return to the Estherea, although next time we will try and visit in warmer weather!

<Author>Arthaus
<Content>Great location,Great staff Like many others my wife and I chose this hotel on the basis of reviews found on Tripadvisor. We were far from disappointed. Our room was on the fourth floor and we were given a canal view at no extra charge. The room was small but one has to remember that one is staying in a city centre town house. The room was very tastefully decorated and the bathroom was more than adequate with plenty of hot water to soak those tired limbs. We stayed four nights between 15-19th March 2007 and from the outset could not have asked for more helpful and conscientious staff. Advice was given as to a good restaurant on the night we arrived. Our flight had been delayed and it was 2145 by the time we booked into the hotel. The staff made the reservation for us whilst we freshened up and were also happy to make reservations for our choices over the following nights. The lobby of the hotel and surrounding lounge and bar are very comfortable and again very pleasing to the eye. I read previous moans about the breakfast and yes if you look around you will I'm sure find cheaper deals. However the hotel restaurant is cosy, with nice tablecloths and pottery and the choice of food and drink is plentiful (14 Euros per Head)The location is excellent being centrally located. Everwhere is within walking distance, but importantly the hotel is surrounded by great eating establishments. Directly behind the hotel is one of the best fish restaurants one could hope for. Lucius, Spuistraat 247. We went twice it was that good. Not cheap, but plenty of atmosphere and bistro appearance. Casa di David further along Singel from the hotel provided great Italien food, but recommend you book particularly on a week-end. Good, wholesome Dutch food at Haesje Claes, again behind the hotel, along from Lucius. Cafe Gommel around the corner (left out the hotel down the alley) is a great old bar and try the Cheeseboard for a good snack at just over 4 Euros. Finally, fresh pitta bread at the Greek adjacent to the hotel is well worth a visit.To example the great efforts of the staff, my wife lost both her wedding and eternity ring whilst in Amsterdam. We reported this to the reception, where before long one ring had been recovered from one of the washing machines in the laundry. The following day, the staff had recovered the second ring and seemed as happy as we were.Don't stay anywhere else in Amsterdam

<Content>beautiful hotel, but... This hotel has a fantastic location on the Singel canal within walking distance to the major attractions in Amsterdam. The lobby and public areas are beautiful. <Content>Beautiful hotel wonderfully located This was my husband's and my 10th visit to Amsterdam. We travel there often for business and occasionally on our way home from another European cities. Each time we try to find a location in which we can call 'home' and return to each time we have to be in the city. We have found our 'home' in the Estherea. The staff were wonderful. <Author>VanGoghIII
<Content>Almost perfect My wife and I stayed here from the 14th to the 17th of February and we really loved almost every aspect of it. In a beautiful situation overlooking a nice canal, it has a nice reception area, a beautiful marine fishtank with the most gorgeously brightly coloured fish, friendly staff, and somewhere nice to sit and have a drink after a night out. To be honest, neither myself or my wife slept particularly comfortably in the beds despite other people commenting on how nice they were, but I never normally sleep well in hotels so that's not really a fault in my opinion. What wasn't a good thing though was having a load of scaffolding outside the window, and a pair of Dutch workmen having a bit of a natter before starting work, quite early in the morning. We solved this problem by paying the extra to get a room with a nice view over the canal, but no offer of a discount was made, and no mention of the work in progress was advised to us at booking, and I do feel as though we were taken advantage of a little bit as regards that. Once we'd paid the extra, and got the new room, we had a lovely stay, but sorry, it left a negative that hasn't gone after 3 weeks.

<Author>Donk-Argyle
<Content>Great hotel, even with kids With kids aged 9, 7 and 4, finding the right hotel with inter-connecting or adjacent rooms is vital. Despite having been promised this, the rooms we were given were separated by an internal courtyard and some distance apart, albeit neighbouring.The next day, we were offered alternative rooms which were right next to each other and from this moment on, we had a fantastic stay. The hotel was excellent with really friendly staff who used their initiative and for whom nothing was any trouble.Rooms were very good, well-equipped and very attractive. Worth getting rooms with a view if you can, not on the internal courtyard so you have natural light.Breakfast was not cheap at 14 euros each, but it was good and free for children under 12.The location is great with good access to tourist attractions and a variety of good local restaurants.This was our first visit to Amsterdam and it is a great city, even with kids. All the main sites are worth visiting and many are free for the children except Nemo which was 11.50 euros each. Riding the trams and walking the canals alone are worth the journey!The hotel was undergoing re-decoration whilst we were staying and the weather was pretty poor, even by UK standards, and despite this, we had a great time and would have no hesitation in recommending the hotel.

<Author>SaschaManchester
<Content>Fantastic hotel- shame about the building work Stayed at the hotel Estherea after reading excellent reviews on trip advisor. I travel a lot and am always a bit dubious about trusting reviews but this really is an excellent hotel, one of the best boutique hotels I have stayed in. The decor is elegant but the hotel is very relaxed with a friendly and cosy ambiance. Our room had been very recently renovated and was immaculate combining traditional decor, furniture and comforts with all the modern extras you would expect from a discerning hotel including an LCD flat screen.  Unfortunately for us as our room was so newly renovated,the room next door was in the process of being renovated which we found out as we were awoken at 7.30am to the sounds of drilling and sawing!. Was very very disapointed that a hotel with such apparant high standards would not have pre warned us of the buiding work at such close proximity, especially as I had e-mailed the hotel just 2 days earlier. The hotel were appologetic but only after I had approached them and I was compensated but would have rather enjoyed a more relaxing stay. Would still rate this hotel very highly as the buiding work is coing to an end, and guests arriving after the renovations are complete will have a wonderfull stay, however, if your stay is soon, I would check with the hotel before your arrival to avoid dissapointment. The hotel is idealy located for all attractions and there are some great neighbourhood resteraunts and bars. In particualr Casa di david @ Singel 420, about 5 mins walk, is an excellent Italian.

<Author>aabeesley
<Content>Gem of a Hotel We stayed here for a long weekend at the end of January. Although I had read the reviews I was still a little nervous about the hotel, however upon arrival I was really pleasantly surprised. We arrived to a typical Amsterdam street, narrow with a canal and our hotel was a couple of the traditional houses converted. The reception staff were really friendly and we were upgraded to a deluxe room. Our room was lovely (room 216) with a lovely view overlooking the canal. It was immaculately clean, spacious with a extra large bathroom. If you a planning on staying I would recommend that you upgrade to a deluxe room and if possible ask for this room as our friends who were also staying in a deluxe room didn't get such a nice room - again overlooking the canal but not as large and a small bathroom. Another thing which I really liked was the bed linen, nice fluffy pillows and a lovely duvet, no horrible blankets. There was building work going on whilst we were staying however it didn't affect our stay. The location of this hotel is perfect. Literally just around the corner from Dam Square. I would definitely return to Amsterdam and to this hotel.

<Author>Peanut85
<Content>Fantastic Hotel We stayed at the Estherea for three nights in January 07. We had room 110 which was a canal view room (we were upgraded for free from a standard room). <Author>sixlegsup
<Content>A Gem This hotel is definitely a looker. Eye catching lobby area, beautifully appointed and adorned. Very cozy, the kind of place where you can sit, chat and drink till late in the evening. The rooms were equally as charming and a decent size for Amsterdam. The service was helpful and ambitious, providing directions, a decent hair dryer and generally trying to be one step ahead of our needs.The hotel is a little noisy. Not due to the clientel, but the generally tight quarters and fairly thin walls. If you require absolute quiet to catch 40 winks then you may need to mention this when you book. Also, the hotel is currently undergoing renovations. Unfortunately, we were not informed of this prior to booking or check-in and the work often started prior to 9:00.The hotel sits on a lovely canal and has some great cafes and restaurants nearby. The Luden quickly became one of our favorites. It is also just a few blocks from Dam Square and is generally centrally located to the city sights.Would rate 3 and a half, but will curve down due to the construction. Just came from a 4 star hotel in Paris and this does not quite reach that level, though the service is probably some of the best around.

<Author>leighdd
<Content>Welcome to the Hotel Estherea... I stayed here with my 13 year old daughter, in January. This proved to be a really excellent choice. We had a room on the 5th floor, very quiet, well appointed and a large bathroom, by European standards. We did not opt to pay extra for a canal view-we were only there to sleep anyway !The public rooms downstairs were fabulous- comfortable, spacious and welcoming. The biscuits, sweets, and beverages on tap in the foyer were most appreciated.Front desk staff were most helpful, and always went the extra mile-they lent me an umbrella when it started raining, a cellphone recharger when mine packed up, and were spot on with their restaurant recommendations. Do try the Casa Di David, just 2 blocks down Singel straat, for the best Italian food in Amsterdam.Locationwise this is hard to beat- 5 minutes walk from Dam Square, Kalverstraat, Palace etc. We took the shuttle bus service from Schippol,and found it convenient, and good value for money.My only gripe about our stay there was the exorbitantly high internet charges- 5 Euros for 30 mins just isnt justifiable in in city in the world !Overall, a fantastic little gem, we will definitely be back !

<Author>memnj
<Content>Lovely experience in this charming hotel Stayed 3 nights at Hotel Estherea, and thought it was wonderful.Our pretty, very clean, room faced the Singel Canal, so the views were great. The staff was very courteous, the lobby was lovely and it was very nice to sit and enjoy the coffee and tea that is provided. Location is great, with excellent restaurants just behind the hotel on Spuistraat: Haesje Claes, D'Vijff Vlieghen and Kanttjil  de Tijger were our favorites. Centrally located for walking to the sights (don't miss the floating flower market on Singel Canel at Muntplein.)Can get a little noisy at times, creaking floors, people traffic on the street below, but it didn't detract from all the charm.Word of advice: when taking a taxi (we took one to the airport) we were told by the front desk that if the hotel calls, it is a fixed rate, yet when we got to the airport, we had a hard time with the taxi driver, who seemed not to know a thing about it. Check the cost with the driver first. This was not the hotels fault, however. All in all, a charming hotel and a good value, and I would definitely stay here again when in Amsterdam.

<Author>SargeantPepper
<Content>Beautiful hotel Stayed for 3 nights, booked through Opodo online which was cheapest deal i could find that included breakfast. A good 10 min walk from train station!Really impressed with reception and decor, felt very relaxed with the place. Our room was spacious and very clean. We faced the back of the hotel overlooking a small street. I did request an upgrade with a canal view but i was told this was an extra 40 euros per night. So i declined. Bathroom was nice decor ,very small but with deep bath and shower. Breakfast good, also you can have breakie in your room free of charge which was lovely. Tea/coffee not in room but available 24 hours in reception. Help yourself. Also biscuits, fruit and toffees! We arrived late so ate at Italian directly behind hotel which was good for cheap food.We also dined at a traditional dutch restaurant along the same street called Haasje claes, which was fabulous. You need to book table there is was rammed. cost for two people 3 courses and good bottle of wine 拢58. There was a great atmosphere and the people were very friendly. Hotel was great location and withing easy walking distance to most of sights and Dam square and shops. Just around corner is a tiny bar that sells loads of different beers. We went there twice! We didnt go on trams so walked everywhere, but did do a canal boat which was nice change and gave us a rest.We had a lovely romantic break and the hotel was individual and charming with modern facilities. This beats any chain hotels.Get to tourist attractions early to avoid queues.

<Author>UKNomads
<Content>Ignore any bad reviews - this hotel is all you need!! We're struggling to find fault with the Hotel Estherea. We stayed for three nights and found the staff extremely friendly and helpful.You'll find cheaper, but you'll struggle to beat the location. We didn't have to use public transport to get anywhere as everything is within a 10 minute walk. However, the hotel is far enough away from the centre of Amsterdam to have the peace that we wanted and that some of the cheaper hotels cannot provide. Breakfast at the hotel was not included in the rate but as other reviews state there is a great little cafe within a few yards which does the job for half the price (and this is even mentioned in the hotel guest book!). We tried the hotel breakfast on the last day as well and it was certainly worth the money and kept us going until the middle of the afternoon. The hotel also recommend a number of restaurants and we tried three of these within a few minutes walk and have to agree with the recommendations. Overall, we took cheap flights to see Amsterdam but didn't want a cheap noisy hotel. The Hotel Estherea provided us with everything it promised and we will be recommending it to friends and family and would return without hesitation.

<Author>LunaDeMargarita
<Content>Definitely overrated After seeing so many wonderful reviews on this website, I was determined to book a room there for a three-day stay in Amsterdam. I contacted the hotel directly, and was offered 2 rooms (one for my husband and me, the other - for my 17  20 year olds). Two days before arrival, I e-mailed the hotel to reconfirm the reservation, and specifically asked for 2 rooms facing the canal. Yes, the location of the hotel is superb, and a little family-run restaurant on the corner just outside is wonderful, but the rooms... please! We were given 2 rooms, neither one of which faced the street. The term tiny does not even begin to describe it, and the fact that it was July - hot, humid - and the room had no air conditioning... The staff gave us one small desk fan per room, and we asked for another one because it was sheer hell sleeping in a stuffy, airless room, but were politely told that there were no more fans left to lend. I repeatedly asked to be moved to another room, but was told that the hotel was fully booked and my request could not be honored. In short, our stay at Hotel Estherea was disappointing, but walking the streets of this beautiful city, seeing all the wonderful sights, taking canal rides - it all made up for our not-so-wonderful accommodations.

<Author>RATSOMATIC
<Content>Excellent hotel, great location Just returned from a great 3 night stay in Amsterdam. We had a family room which was comfortable and clean. The lobby has an old fashioned luxurious feel with a library, leather armchairs, chandeliers and a great aquarium. The reception staff were all helpful and friendly. Tea, coffee, hot chocolate and biscuits on tap all day. The upstairs corridors were a bit uninspiring but that was really the only thing that struck me. The hotel is in a great location, on a quiet part of the Singel, a few miniutes walk from Dam square and the main shopping streets, but also close to the quirky shops and boutiques of the Jordaan area. Would definitely return.

<Author>Stragics
<Content>Absolutely Excellent! My husband and I stayed at the Estherea from September 18-22, 2006. From reading tripadvisor posts, I expected the hotel to be great and it lived up to that expectation. Paying 124 Euro/night including breakfast but not a 5% tax (visit the utell website for their Great Rates), I felt that we really came away with one of the best hotel deals in Europe.Upon checking-in, I asked for a room on the 5th floor (none available). I proceeded to ask for a canal view (available for a 45 Euro/night suppliment). We stuck with our original room which was Room 217. The man at the desk told us our room was nice. I thought that was his way of consoling me for not choosing to upgrade to the canal view.However, the room WAS nice! And we were escorted there by a bellboy who carried our bag and showed us how to operate the lights and open the minibar in the room. The room has an entry way with a closet and luggage area on the left and double doors leading to the bathroom on the right. There is no air conditioning in the room, however, there are two small fans provided. There are a few English channels on the tv. The windows opened out onto the most beautiful street view. The bed was two twins pushed together, however, the bed and linens were amazingly comfortable. Soft pillows and two twin-size down comforters made it hard to leave the bed in the morning. The bathroom was incredible and only slightly smaller than the size of the hotel room we had just stayed at in Paris. Double sinks and a deep soaking tub were nice touches. There was always hot water and strong shower pressure when bathing. Both the bathroom and bedroom were kept clean.Service was excellent. From making restaurant reservations to giving directions and train timetables, the staff went out of their way to help us enjoy our time in Amsterdam. The coffee, tea, and hot chocolate machines downstairs were fantastic and the little cookies in their own drawer made a quick snack with the drinks.Breakfast was included in our rate and always hit the spot. Breakfast included: scrambled eggs, hard boiled eggs, bacon, sausage, various breads, cereals, yogurts, fruits, meats, and cheeses. To drink, you'll find a variety of juices, milk, coffee, tea, or hot chocolate. They'll even make you a cappucino if you ask. I believe breakfast is 16 euro if not included in your rate. The breakfast room can hold 60 people and it did get almost full on the Friday morning we were leaving.The location of the hotel is fantastic. We came to Amsterdam via Paris on the Thalys train into Centraal Station. It was approximately a 15 minute walk from the station pulling our suitcase. Going out at night was also very easy and there is much to see within walking distance of the hotel.It would be very hard for me to stay at any other hotel in Amsterdam now that I know how great the Estherea is.  
<Date>Oct 2, 2006

It is close to everything, only a few minutes walk to all the bar action of Leidesplein, shopping, and the flowermarket. The great thing is you can enjoy the noise and the action when you want it, and return to the quiet and calm of this hotel when you are done. The canal view is gorgeous. The room was very clean and adequate. Of course a bit small, but a decent size for a dutch hotel. Staff were extremely kind and helpful. Having a nice complimentary cup of coffee in the lobby lounge after a long day of being out made it feel like home. My one tip, if you know you are going for next year, book this hotel soon, it fills up fast. I will definitely stay there again. It was my husband's first time in Amsterdam, and the hotel was a big hit.

<Author>Vipers
<Content>Excellent Hotel If you want a hotel in Amsterdam which is clean and tidy, has friendly staff, has excellent facilities, and is in an ideal location (i.e. close enough to the action of Leidseplein  Dam Square whilst being far enough away to avoid the more 'undersirable' areas of the city), then the Estherea is for you.On arriving you almost feel you're in a time-warp, with an austere lobby/bar area reminiscent of the 1940's (some would call it charm ?), however this seems to be the whole point of the hotel as it is a perfect deterrent for the ubiquitous hen/stag party element which is more suited to the lesser hotels scattered around the Central Station.As with previous reviews we avoided the Hotel breakfasts  opted for 'Broodjes Bert' cafe which is 30 yards up the road - excellent breakfasts in the open air (weather permitting) for Eu 7.00. Any negatives ? Prices of alcoholic beverages at the bar were a bit excessive (which probably explains why nobody seemed to use it), however I'm probably being picky. Overall, I'd 100% recommend the hotel for any of you over 40 (if you're twenty-something and on an Amsterdam weekend which involves excessive alcohol  partying, this probably isn't the place for you).

<Author>andeesue
<Content>Estherea is a gem! Spent 6 nights in this charming hotel, July 4-10, 2006. Our first room was on the 3rd floor, facing an inner area. It was a warm time and our first night was uncomfortable.The very helpful bellboy suggested we find out if a room is available on the a/c 5th floor, which we did. Apparently, the entire hotel will eventually all be air conditioned. That made all the difference! Our room, though small, was very efficiently arranged, with closets, drawers, built in niches by the beds. Our first room was larger and had a big bathroom, but the canal view and a/c were much more important. We appreciated the ever present fruit available, as well as the coffee/tea/hot chocolate machine, and the cookies and candies.... fun to have a drink at the bar and enjoy the extra treats at no cost. The location is great, and close to many restaurants and places of interest. We took the trams often, and really got around easily. Our friend was staying at a hotel with an enormous amount of stairs just to get to the lobby. I felt we were in the lap of luxury compared to her place. The Estherea is a very special place!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good hotel, Great location WE chose the Estherea based on earlier TripAdvisor reviews and were not disappointed. My wife  I stayed for 5 nights in mid-July after completeing a Baltic cruise. It was fairly warm in Amsterdam and our second floor front canal view room (#210) had no A/C but the nights cooled off quickly and the provided fan helped considerably. We slept with open windows and although it could get noisy with canal boats and mopeds, it get quite quiet after 10 pm (11 on Friday night) so sleep wasn't a problem.It is a lovely, mostly residential/small offce area with loads of cafes and restaurants on Spuistrasse, the street behind the hotel as well as in the nearby Dam Square and Leidesplein areas. We especially liked the prix fixe menu at Luden as well as the more bistro-like Cafe Luxembourg.The hotel's breakfast was fine, better than many European hotels and 'only' eur14 (where many charge eur20 or more).I would definitely recommend this hotel based on its location and helpful, friendly staff.

<Author>snooper
<Content>Wonderful Hotel We stayed at this charming hotel July 4th thru the 6th on our way back from a cruise in the Baltic. We had booked a room on the canal which was on the second floor. It was very beautifully decorated with lovely drapes, and wonderful molding on the ceiling. The bathroom was spacious and had a wonderful deep tub with shower. The only problem was that Amsterdamn was experiencing a heat wave with temperatures in the 90's. This of course was not the hotel's fault and we were lucky to be quick enough to put our request in to move to the fifth floor which did have air conditioning. There is also an elevator which is not always the case in these small hotels. The staff especially the bellman/porter was wonderful and gave us great recommendations for places to eat. We would stay there again but would book a room on the fifth floor not on the canal side as it can be quite noisy. The hotel has a nice little bar and breakfast room. We walked down the street (Singel) and had breakfast at a little cafe which only charged 7 euros for ham and eggs on a roll with tomatoes and fruit on the side, wonderful coffee also. There is also a great greek deli next door with fantastic food and very reasonable. This hotel is in the canal ring and you can walk to the central station from there.  
<Date>Jul 10, 2006

<Author>CATRAVEL
<Content>A decent place Stayed in the hotel 3 days ago. We typically stay in 4 or 5 star hotels and resorts and while not being picky, we know when the place is decent, fake or a rip off with a storefront. We really liked this hotel for it's location, staff and ambience. The place is not really that small but retains the boutique hotel atmosphere. Stayed on the 5th floor, top floor attic- like room (# 514) facing a canal. The room was not large but functional and charming with large bath, safe, and mini bar. Complimentary coffee, tea, cocoa, fruit and snacks next to the lobby. Quiet canal street location in great neighborhood, only 2 blocks (5 min. walk) from the ground zero of Amsterdam, 10 minute walk (average pace) to Red Light District. The street in the back has plenty of good restaurants. We tried 2 restaurants recommended by the hotel in their room booklet and liked them both. Massage can be arranged by the hotel. The bell boy even carried a massage table for the lady that showed up. Front desk was very helpful. Just friendly people all around. The bottom line: very reasonable for the price. Beware of some Chinese and Middle Eastern/North African restaurants in the area which serve substandard food for inflated prices... with a smile, of course. Stick to what is recommended by the hotel or just use common sense by picking a place that is busy (not only with beer drinkers) and appears to have a professional setup. There are a lot of tourists in the area and bad restaurants don't really care about repeat business. Anyway, next time in Amsterdam we don't have to look for another place to stay.

<Content>Stay here!!! We spent a wonderful 3 days at this Hotel of which I highly recommend. If you arrive by train at Central Station you will not need to take anymore transport if you are staying at the beautiful Estherea as it is only a 15 minute walk from the station, 5minute walk from Dam Square and within 5-15 minute walk from the main attractions of the city i.e. Anne Frank house, Van Gogh museum etc. The Hotel is truly beautiful, with wonderful staff who always have a smile and friendly welcome for you. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the Elegant Estherea Have just returned from our European holiday, and am more and more convinced about the advantages of staying at family run hotels.The beautiful Estherea hotel is a family run hotel on the quiet Singel canal in the heart of amsteredam. The main shopping and nightlife areas i.e. Dam square, Leidseplein etc. are a few steps away and one can never imagine that the hustle and bustle is so close to this tranquil and pretty neighbourhood.The hotel itself is classy and elegant, and the beautiful reception and bar area with its rich furnishing and beautiful furniture resembles an upper class country home, warm and inviting. The stunning aquarium in the reception area which my daughter fell in love with, is lovingly tended too by the owner himself. We were met at the door by the friendliest porter in the world (he helps at the bar too), and he pretty much set the tone for the rest of the staff who were extremely corteous and helpful.The room was bright airy and plain lovely, with great use of space and very rich tapestry. The beds were very comfortable and the linen of good quality. The bathroom, although slightly small, had all one required , fluffy fresh towels and complimentry toilettries of good quality. Needless to say, everything was very clean. The complimentry coffee, tea and hot chocolate facility (all day long} near the reception, alongwith fresh fruit and cakes was very welcome as we would pop in and out of the hotel with our shopping bags. A nice touch indeed !!Definately recommend this hotel and would absolutely stay here again when i re-visit Amsterdam.
