<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Absolutely wonderful stay I spent 3 nights (June 1-4) at Estherea with a friend. Never been in an Amsterdam hotel before but the reputation of hotels there it's quite bad, therefore - after careful consideration of other Tripadvisor's members! - opted for it, especially after getting an excellent rate through the Otel site. The Hotel is in an excellent position, about 5 minutes walk from Dam Square (possibily the busiest and noisiest place in Amsterdam!) but it's located on a lovely, tree-shaded canal street and therefore has a pleasant, quiet location. Indeed it's so centrally located that we never took a tram during our stay to wander around the whole of the city centre! Even the Central Station is about 15 minutes walk (if your luggage isn't too heavy of course, otherwise it's just a short trip with tram). The room we got (511) was on fifth floor and in the back side, therefore absolutely quiet. It was reasonably dimensioned (not a large room but we managed to find a place for 2 luggages and 2 backcpacks without bumping on them at every step). Everything was spotlessly clean, most importantly the bathroom, where towels got changed every day. The service was awesome, people at the door always smiling, courteous and full of help. Also the buffet breakfast was plentiful and of good quality (several different types of bread, good brands for jam and cornflakes, etc.); there was also free availabitlity at all time of coffee/tea from a machine behind the main lobby, which was very welcome after a day of walking in the cool air of this fake summer! I will definitely choose again the Estherea if I will return to Amsterdam!

<Author>AHLS
<Content>Loved the Estherea Lovely hotel in a quiet but central location on the Singel canal. Only 3 or 4 minutes walk from Dam Square. We (2 adults  2 children) spent 3 nights in a quad room on the 4th floor, with 2 sets of twin beds. The room overlooked Spuistraat rather than the Singel canal, but it was a good size, light and airy, with an ensuite bathroom. Room was spotlessly clean and had a TV with UK channels. Safe in room for valuables. Breakfast buffet was from 7.00 - 10.00 and included continental breakfast, fruit, and cooked. Breakfast was Euro 14 for adults but free for children and good quality and value. Free coffee, tea and hot chocolate available from reception area until 11.00 pm. Small bar near reception. Staff were friendly and helpful. No restaurant in the hotel for evening meals but we ate at a couple of restaurants recommended by the hotel within 5 minutes walk (Casa di David on Singel and Haesje Claes on Spuistraat) and both were very good. We would certainly stay at the Estherea if we visited Amsterdam again

<Author>Modern_Phrenologist
<Content>Good small hotel in excellent location My wife and I spent 6 nights at the Estherea. It is a fine hotel, in an excellent location with a friendly, helpful, knowledgeable staff. Our room was rather large by European standards and was the only room in the hotel with a balcony. The balcony was lovely for the 15 minutes each day it did not rain. The bathroom was compact, but had everything one could need, including the expected soaps, shampoos, etc. My only reservation is the cost and quality of the breakfasts. At 14 Euros per person it was not good value for money. Much better could be had in neighborhood cafes.The location is excellent, within easy walking distance of most of the mian sights and museums in Amsterdam. Since it is only about 200 yards from the nearest tram stop, it is easy to travel anywhere else in the city. There are more than a dozen restaurants, of various price ranges and foods, within two blocks of the hotel and many more if one walks 3 or 4 blocks.We would certainly stay in the hotel again and would recommend it to friends.

<Author>lochnagar
<Content>Good location and comfortable, but... We stayed at this hotel for 3 nights and our family had four rooms - all very comfortable and quite spacious. We were visiting Amsterdam for a family member's birthday. My wife and I were in a twin room on the fourth floor and our two children stayed in another twin on the same floor. The hotel staff were very helpful, particularly the night desk attendant. We arrived quite late and he was very efficient. The 14 Euro breakfast was okay but not very memorable for the price.One issue which did concern us was that someone in the room next to our children was using cannabis - the smell pervaded all over the fourth floor. We complained to the hotel management who apparently, knew that someone had been using because the cleaners had seen the evidence. The hotel info booklet says quite clearly that they do not allow drugs in the hotel and the management told us that the fourth floor was a no smoking floor anyway. They didn't seem very anxious to enforce their own rules. The hotel was clean and comfortable and is in a good location. Would go back again, providing they sort out their confusing smoking/non-smoking policy.  
<Date>May 23, 2006

<Author>dd01a
<Content>Stop Sneaking in to our Room! Anywhere you go, perhaps the bottom line is you only get what you paid for... We chose this hotel because of the popularity on this site, but went for a 500 Euro for 3 nights (standard double) special deal. Upon arrival we (cheakily) asked for a canal view room but was told there would be 45 Euro supplement charge per night.So our cheap-rate room was on the 2nd level with no view. Instead there was a small, dark patio right outside our window and a few workmen appeared every morning - God knows what they were renovating - checking up  down outside walls. We kept the curtains shut but had to keep the windows open while we were in, as the room was quite stuffy and the bathroom had no ventilation (there was a tiny, tiny one which didn't seem to do the job at all)The walls  ceilings were so thin - we couldn't hear the next door but we could even hear people whispering in the corridor, footsteps on the squeaky floor upstairs were almost unbearable.Peculiar thing was this..... You return the key to the reception everytime you go out, so they know which guests are in or out. On the 1st day when we went out for a dinner, we left some lights on and made sure all our windows were shut (dodgy patio!), came back a couple of hours later to find all the lights turned off and one of the top small windows open. 2nd day while we were out they changed the furniture - changed the bedside table, entire dressing table  all our things in the drawers were taken out (ok but why? we thought we were in the wrong room!) Evening of the 3rd day we deliberately left all the lights on and went out for a meal, came back few hours later to find some lights off, fridge door wide open (again WHY?????) small windows open again...We're not making up the story! And certainly we were not on the magic mushroom or whatever that is!! As soon as we go out they come in to check the room, open the window for ventilation and sneak out! Well there was a safe in the room so we weren't too concerned about the security... Shower was powerful. Free tea/coffee machine at the reception. But then it would have been a lot nicer if there was a kettle facility in each room. The hotel's in the nice part of the city, stunning chandelier  aquerium tank at the reception... The mystery of freaky guestroom-checker remains, but besides that, I would only recommend this hotel if you're prepared to pay more for better rooms.

<Author>UK_Manchester
<Content>Do yourself a favour: Stay there We have just returned today from three nights at the Estherea. We can only echo the opinions of all the previous reviewers who gave it the maximum five yellows as we call them. The staff could not have been more pleasant and helpful. From the moment you walk into the lobby, which exudes its own charm with tasteful decor, you have a sense of stepping back into a more leisurely and refined age. My wife was celebrating a significant birthday and when we were shown into our room the management had left a gift of toiletries wrapped in cellophane on the table. This little personal touch together with the complimentary hot drinks sweets and chocolates show us that the large, soulless chain hotels have much to learn from the smaller, family-run hotels which go the extra mile.Amsterdam is a compact city and whilst the Estherea is in a quiet location it is no more than two or three minutes walk from the bars, restaurants and shops. This is the best of both worlds. The management gives guests a list of recommended restaurants within walking distance. We tried two of them, an Indonesian in Rembrandt Square and a Thai restaurant, both of which were excellent.We feel the hotel maintains high standards and is not overpriced when compared to similar hotels in other Continental cities.The acid test is would we go back to the Estherea. Answer: like a shot.

<Content>Exceellent Hotel! My boyfriend and I have just returned from 3 nights at this Hotel over the Easter break and it was wonderful!Ok so it isn't cheap but, it was well worth the money and I didn't begrudge paying a bit more for a fabulous room which overlooked the Singel Canal and was huge with a wonderful four poster bed.We found the staff extremely helpful and friendly, we left our bags at reception on our last day and were told to help ourselves to the free coffee and tea on our return to pick them up which was a welcome break.The breakfast was expensive at 14 Euros but we only had it the once and it made our Sunday a more relaxing day.We tried to get a cab to the Hotel from Amsterdam Central Station on our arrival but the cab driver obviously felt it wasn't a worthwhile route for him and told us it was only a short walk!! We took the recommendation of eating at the Three Sisters in Rembrandtsplein on Saturday night which Reception booked for us and it was a delicious meal, lovely steak and great service.I would definately stay at this hotel again, it's location is first class and I will certainly recommend it to any of my friends.

<Author>lass=
<Content>A perfect location; good value This was our first visit to Amsterdam and it is hard to believe that we could have selected a better hotel in terms of its central location and the friendliness and helpfulness of its staff.We found the Estherea at TripAdvisor and booked via an agent. We stayed for two nights. When we checked in the total room rate was split unevenly between the first (Thursday) and second (Friday) nights - so it may pay to check rates for a wholly (cheaper) midweek stay if your itinerary allows. We were allowed to check in two hours early and were given a room without a canal view. However, the room was large, spotless and extremely well furnished so no problem there.The free coffee and hot chocolate were very gladly received on several occasions during our stay. If there was a downside with this hotel it was breakfast which was not good value at 14 Euros per person - the juice is not fresh, the cereals are still in the packets and the very limited cooked food was of average quality.Breakfast is the only meal served in the restaurant. Room service is provided by staff ordering from a sandwich bar and restaurant nearby. This appears to be a good policy, at least as far as the restaurant (Haesje Claes)is concerned as, when we tried to eat there, there was a queue leading into the street outside.We tried the hotel's 'favourite' restaurant, as listed in the guide in our room. This is the D'Theeboom which is less than ten minutes walk from the hotel and is on the same canal (Singel). We were so glad we took the recommendation - if we have eaten a better meal in the last ten years, we can't remember it! Get the hotel staff to book for you - we turned up without a reservation and were very lucky to get in.We would definitely recommend The Estherea to anyone visiting Amsterdam. We would certainly stay there again.

<Content>A great hotel experience We spent five nights here, and were happy that we had requested a room on the canal side - not only a beautiful view, but quieter than the back side of the hotel. <Author>apkinguk
<Content>Great Location My boyfriend and I have just returned from a two night stay at the Estheria. It is in a superb location with lovely communal rooms downstairs where you can relax and enjoy the free coffee, tea and fruit. Our room was nice inside the only drawback was the lack of natural light, the window looked out on to an internal 'shaft' along with other rooms so you couldn't really open the curtains; they were also doing work on an adjacent room which was loud at 8.20 am. This said everything else was fine and the breakfast was great. Ours was included in the price (through Expedia- although the city tax is extra on your bill at the end of your stay.. not much though).. There's a lovely little beer place practically on the door step (turn left at hotel exit then take first left down the side road) called Gollem. Try a Jenever (Dutch gin) with a beer chaser.. Dante on Spuistraat a bit further up is also a good watering hole. We had a lovely Indonesian meal near by at Kantjil  De Tijger on Spuistraat 291/293- just order the 'rice table' and see what you get.. wonderful. Also De Jaren (Nieuwe Doelenstraat 20-22) over the Amstel is great for a good view and a bite of lunch. All in all I would recommend this hotel, particularly for the fab location.

<Author>clars
<Content>Nice hotel but not really worth the money Just back from a stay in amsterdam which is a lovely city to visit. It was as a present for my husband so I wanted to get a nice hotel. This one is lovely but definitely not a four star hotel by any means. After reading reviews on this site we didn't go for breakfast..there are lovely places around to get something to eat for far less than 14 euro which is what the hotel charges. We were in room 407 which is too the back but is so noisy..not sure if it was just the people in the other rooms or just the hotel in general. The free tea and coffee and fruit was lovely especially considering it was so cold. The reception staff were really friendly and the location is lovely. I had asked by email for directions to the hotel and was told to either get a taxi from the airport or the connexion which connects the airport to the hotels. I wouldn't go for either of these ways...a one way ticket on the train is 3.60 each and then it is about a 15 minute stroll to the hotel. A taxi would cost 42 euro.....There are some really dodgy looking hotels in amsterdam so you have to be careful but this was 300 for the two of us for two nights with no breakfast so I think it was a bit steep.

We didn't complain as our break was only for a few nights and we didn't spend much time in our room but given the choice I wouldn't stay in that particular room again!

<Author>bunyete
<Content>Non smokers beware! I went to Amsterdam for the first time with my spouse last weekend. We stayed at the Estheria for 2 nights in a deluxe room (room #114).At first we were very satisfied by the hotel because it is beautiful, our room was large, clean, well decorated, and had a nice view on the canal, and the staff made a good impression on us.The first problem arose on the first night: our room was on the first floor and we were disturbed around 1a.m by a group of people talking loudly right under our windows, probably waiting for some friends on the doorstep of the hotel. Apparently, nothing special has been done for (external)noise insulation. However it only last 15 minutes and thus was a minor problem. Note that we could not hear any noise coming from other rooms.The second problem was of much greater importance. We asked for a non-smoking room, as usual, because we are, though french, very sensitive (negatively) to cigarette smoke. The room was indeed non-smoking, and nobody had smoked in our room, but the room in front of ours (room #115) was a smoking room. And the guests in room #115, in their right, were unfortunately smoking a lot. Our room was invaded by smoke all night and we had to sleep with an open window in spite of the outside temperature (I would say around -5 掳C). At the reception, after checking the corridor, they admitted that there was indeed a lot of smoke but could not do anything because room #115 was a smoking room and the hotel was full (so that they could not give us another room).We thus spent a terrible second night in that hotel.We however appreciated the breakfast (non smoking area). Note that it is not included in the room price (extra 14 EUR per person).Note also that the hotel has no restaurant but that there are plenty right next to it.I did not ask for any discount (not my style, at least with my wife standing next to me :C), but when I checked out, they did not ask me whether I had enjoyed my stay, they did not apologize, and did not offer any kind of compensation.Apart from that, Amsterdam is a beautiful city and we had a wonderful time wandering in its streets and visiting a few of its museums.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>17th century canalhouse charm My girlfriend and I loved the Estherea. This was my second time in Amsterdam, and the hotel was definitely better than where I stayed the first time. PROS1) Central location on Singel, which is the innermost of Amsterdam's four concentric canals. Roughly 3 blocks from Dam Square, with easy access to virtually all Amsterdam attractions. You can walk anywhere from here or catch a tram, but if you have luggage, a taxi is Eur 10 or less from Amsterdam Centraal. 2) Very attractive lobby with extensive sitting areas, a big aquarium, and all the charm of a 17th century Dutch canalhouse. 3) Well-decorated room with soft lighting, a soft off-orange paint job, and very comfortable bed.4) Responsive management. We had a billing problem that was very quickly resolved by management.5) Informative website with detailed property history.CONS1) Breakfast is 14 Euro extra. We skipped it. There are dozens of quaint little cafes within a 10-minute walk of the hotel, most of which have English menus and good breakfasts for Eur 6/person. Just walk in the direction of Jordaan.2) Bath amenities. You'll encounter quintessential Dutch cheapness when there is no soap, shampoo, or conditioner in the bathroom. Instead, there is a wall-mounted bottle of institutional-style chemical ooze that is said to work on both hair and skin. My girlfriend had a rough time, getting neither clean hair nor skin.3) Views. If you want a canal view, be sure to ask for it (and pay extra). Our room had a view of a ventilation shaft and caught a lot of noise from the teenagers across the ventilation shaft. The clientele of the hotel appeared to trend towards college-age Americans and families.Also note: wireless internet is 10 Eur per 24 hours.

<Author>mollysmum
<Content>Fabulous Husband and I stayed at Hotel Estherea from 11th to 13th Jan on our first trip to Amsterdam. Although we had a really hectic schedule and so did not spend a lot of time in the hotel, it really made our stay special.Its location is excellent - very handy for Dam Square, trams to wherever you want to go, and the street behind the hotel is packed with fantastic restaurants (recommend 'Five').There's such a lovely ambience from the moment you enter. Our room (212) had a canal view and was pleasantly and comfortably furnished.We did pay extra for a 'deluxe' room since they told us that was the only way we'd get a canal view, but another couple we met paid the standard rate (98 Euro) and also got a canal view.We also paid for wireless internet access for the first day, but then discovered so many unsecured networks in the vicinity that we didn't pay for access the second day, since we weren't too worried about internet security.The most expensive (reputedly) brothel in Amsterdam is a few doors down, but it's very discreet and the area in general is very upmarket.Highly recommend it (the hotel, that is)!

<Author>lass=
<Content>Excellent Hotel We spent a long weekend in this hotel in September 2005 and found everything we had read in the reviews to be true.The hotel is in a great location for touring Amsterdam and although near the centre you are not disturbed by noise at night.Our room was beautiful and had a lovely view over the canal. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A very nice hotel at a nice price We were very happy with our three night stay at the Estherea. We got an excellent weekend rate of 99Euros/night, and felt we got very good value. They also provide a 5% discount for paying with cash. The hotel is very clean and nicely decorated. As mentioned in other reviews, there is complementary tea and coffee in the lounge and small snacks. They have a library with travel books which we were able to borrow and take to our room to read. Our room had no view at all - looking into a window-well, but was large and very clean. There is really nothing negative to say for the rate we paid.

<Author>Brissie-Student
<Content>Too beautiful for just 1 night I was recommended this hotel by my travel agent. After reading ALL the reviews at Tripadvisor, I was rather looking forward to seeing the place for myself. I stayed just 1 night in this beautiful hotel. I was fortunate enough to get a room with a canal view and a double bed just for me!! The staff were friendly enough, though I received a somewhat cold and confused reception on my initial arrival. My room looked like it was recently renovated, although the door looked like someone had tried to break into it. At the lobby there was ample FREE muffins, pastries, tea and coffee. The ONLY downside was that I was misled into thinking that the hotel wasn't far from the Centraal train station - in fact, it took me close to 30mins of walking (with luggage and backpack)! *phew* Overall, it was more than sufficient for my purpose - a place just to shower and sleep. I'd love to go back there in the future.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Lovely place to stay Having read all the excellent reviews on Trip Advisor I was confident we had chosen a good hotel and we were not disappointed. As the trip was to celebrate a birthday I had requested a canal view room. Although we did not have a canal view we were given a great room on the top floor with a balcony and the staff even gave a small present on arrival.From photos I have seen some of the rooms are on the small side, (although our room was a good size), BUT as a tourist out for most of the day how much space do you need? Our room (as well as the lobby, lounge area and restaurant) was spotlessly clean, richly decorated and had more charm than all of the large chain hotels put together. The hotel was on a quiet canal away from the busy/noisy streets but within easy walking distance of most places of interest and some nice restaurants and cafes. If I ever return to Amsterdam I will certainly stay there again.

<Author>MrandMrsTee
<Content>Great location, nice hotel We stayed at The Estherea for 6 nights in April 2005. The best thing about the hotel is its location, but that's not to say that it is the only good thing about it. But first things first.Adjoining the Spui, in the inner part of the Western Canal Belt on the Singel, near the Jordaan, near the Beginhof, with many excellent restaurants, bars, coffee shops, shopping areas and major tram access all within very close walking distance, it is probably as well located a hotel as there is in Amsterdam. It is amazing that this place can maintain relative quiet but it does. The rooms are small, but clean, with very nice bathrooms. The first room we were taken to was not exactly to our liking (though we would have been fine had they not been willing to let us change) but the staff was very nice and made a room change to a room that was more to our liking with little effort. Both rooms had canal views. They offer free coffee, tea and hot chocolate (available 24/7), they have a nice bar and a breakfast room with a typical dutch buffet breakfast (we didn't eat there -- we chose to eat breakfast at several nearby places that gave a much better slice of local experience). The hotel has apparently been owned by the same family for a long time, and it is pretty obvious -- much of the staff seemed related to one another. We were very happy there, more for the location than the rooms themselves, but there were nice amenities, nice rooms and excellent value for the money (and the location is definitely superior to many far more expensive and only marginally nicer hotels). At the end of 6 nights, we weren't sick of the place, which also says something.A word to those who care about such things. The Estherea is not cannibas friendly -- they politely but firmly make it clear that cannibas smoking is not allowed in the hotel. However, being within a block of Tweed Kamer, one of the most interesting and eclectic coffee shops in Amsterdam, and several others as well, it really didn't matter. Cheers!  
<Date>Jul 15, 2005

<Author>Ellapbfm
<Content>Lovely traditional hotel, with great staff Me and my boyfriend stayed here for our anniversary last weekend and we had an excellent time. The hotel is in a perfect location in the Canal Singel and is close enough to walk to all the attractions, museums, bars and restaurants but far enough to be able to leave the red light district and coffee shops behind! It is also close enough to walk to from the Centraal Train Station.Although our room 313 had neither a canal or a street view and it was slightly small it was beautifully decorated and had everything we needed. We are used to staying in hostels and slighlty more budget hotels so this was luxurious! We didnt go for the breakfast on top of the room as at 14 euros each per day we thought it a little expensive and we dont usually eat much breakfast anyway so we left that. But there are free drinks; water, tea, coffee and hot chocolate and also free fruit which we had a lot of so that was very useful and saved a few pennies. I chose this hotel through the reviews on this website and the only concern I had was about the staff. I would just like to stay that I found ALL of the staff polite and nice, they helped us with dinner recommendations and reservations and when they found out it was our anniversary the lady on Reception ( I think her name was Esselaar, apologies for the bad spelling!) arranged to have some goodies taken up to our room in lovely packaging and a nice note, which was really really nice of them!So I would highly recommend this hotel to any couples wanting to go away to a nice quiet hotel, there were a few screaming kiddies running around but I think its mainly for adults. I would definitely go back to stay there if I were to go back to Amsterdam and will be recommending it to any friends, family or colleagues that go to Amsterdam.

<Author>weenie
<Content>liked it for the most part We stayed at Hotel Estherea May 9-12th. for the most part I agree with everything that has been written about the hotel. great location, it has been recently renovated and is quite lovely, close to shopping and restaurants etc. The tea/cofee station is a great plus in the lobby. The ambience in the lobby is pleasant and welcoming. Breakfast is okay, nothing special. I did wish they served even a light dinner as we were travelling with elderly parents and this would have suited them quite nicely some nights.Here are some other things that we did not like.My in-laws stayed in room 412 which overlooked the canal, the room is small but adequate and they enjoyed it. Overall they found it quiet enough for sleeping with the exeption of one night when people were quite rowdy for sometime in a boat in the canal below them. My husband, daughter and I had a triple - room 419 which overlooked the back of the hotel. not the most pleasant view, walls of graffiti etc. The main problem was the noise all night long of cars flying past the window and the voices from the street may as well have been in our room. we did not sleep well at all and one night not all. The room was very nice, our daughter had a pull out bed from the wall which was very comfortable as was our bed. I definitely would not stay in that room again.The bathroom is quite small, even for European size. There was nowhere to put toilitries etc but that was not a huge deal.The main thing that I did not like was the front desk staff. there was an older gentleman (I believe already mentioned in former reviews) who was verging on rude. I truly believed he thought he was there for reasons other than serving the customer. he was very unapproachable and gave the impression as you walked towards him that he would rather have disappeared. There was also a young lady on the desk who was very abrasive and had a very take it or leave it attitude. I saw them make fun of the customer behind their back on more than one occasion. something they should be more aware of.On the positive side there was a bar man who has been with the hotel for 6 months, regretfully we did not get his name. He was excellent and went far beyond customer service with a very pleasant attitude. He truly seemed to like his job.I will say that my husband became ill while we were there with a fever and infected throat and they were very good at getting a doctor, and when I asked for some toast to be sent up they sent up a tray of snacks all complimentary and wished him a speedy recovery.Over all we enjoyed staying at this hotel but I will say I was put off with the haughtiness of these two reception staff. someone should remind them that we are the customer and they should demonstrate better customer care. Unfortunately I tended to treat them the way I felt we were being treated so that likely did not help matters. Finally I would like to stay here again but only if we could be guaranteed a quieter room, and also if they gave their staff some training.  
<Date>May 17, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent location, charming Hotel We just finished a very pleasant stay at the Hotel Estherea from April 23-29. The ideal location on a quiet, lovely canal allowed walking to many sites and easy access to both public transportation and Central Station for daytrips. The public rooms are rich, warm and comfortable with small extras that make a difference- free tea, coffee, hot chocolate and fruit in the lobby, a lending library with english selections. <Author>katkearsley
<Content>Excellent Location I have just returned from a 3 night stay in Amsterdam with 3 female friends. We stayed at this hotel on the strength of the reviews on this site and I can say that I was very pleased with the location and accommodation. The room was spotless if slightly small and the bathroom looked newly renovated and kept clean and well stocked.. Unfortunately the view was not good as the room was back to back with another room about 6 feet away. I asked if there was a room overlooking the canal and was told that the hotel was full. It didn't look full as we saw only a few other people during the weekend but as we didn't spend too much time in the room I guess it wasn't too important anyway. The breakfast room is very pleasant and the meal plentiful and fairly varied - certainly adequate and relaxing. The bonus is the tea, coffee and hot chocolate maker in the lobby with biscuits and chocolates to go with it - help yourself at any time - saves a fortune! the public rooms are very pleasant to sit in. But the great thing is the location - within easy walking distance to main tourist areas and train station but very quiet and peaceful - no rowdiness at all. Hotel recommends some great restaurants and will also book them for you - very helpful staff. I work in a travel agency and would have no problems recommending this hotel to any customer.

<Author>Keith_Richards
<Content>Best Location, Nice Hotel Just got back from a 4-day trip to Amsterdam, stayed at the Hotel Estherea and was relieved it came good - nice location on a leafy part of the Singel Canal (10-15 minutes walk from just about everything). This was my first trip to Amsterdam and was pleased I hadn't booked anywhere near Dam Square - if you want to do the bars/restaurants/museums and wake up to a great breakfast on the canal that's typically 'post-card' Amsterdam... then The Estherea won't disappoint (If you want to smoke spliffs, then don't book the Estherea - they don't like the smoke/smell effecting everyone else... but I guess 'space-cakes' are OK, whilst we are on this subject... not everyone in Amsterdam is spaced out doing coffee shops - life goes on as in most European cities with the daily work routine the norm for most people... for sure have a good time and if it's your bag to have time out in a coffee shop then this is a good place to have a relaxing time - for the record I don't smoke or drink as much as I did when I was 18-30 and now find myself spending hours in museums/bars/restaurants... something those old folks did, but now I've turned 40 and have children I find it's crept up from behind and I'm slowly turning into a 16 year olds worst nightmare / don't get me wrong... I still like drinking too much but I just can't face the morning afterwards anymore - it takes me a week to recover, mores the pity).The Hotel: I had booked a canal view room for the two of us (left the kids at home / Amsterdam is not really the place for young children on holiday)... I paid the little extra for the canal view... good move - good sized room, great view to wake up to, small bathroom, but clean. The hotel does not have a restaurant, but does have a small bar and a good breakfast room. Recently refurbished to deliver the 4-star welcome, but the room was 3-star... saying that the location was 5-star. Free Tea/Coffee/Hot-Chocolate 24/7... might not be much but makes a huge difference when staying in a hotel and keeping your costs within reason.The Staff: Sorry to say I agree with some of the other remarks... when we arrived the guy on the desk was very cold, but not rude - not typical of Dutch people... but the girls on front of desk during the day very welcoming. The last two days saw a different guy on the desk and he was fine... I would retun to this hotel no problem, I would also recommend staying there if this is your first visit.Location: Can't help banging this one home... have a look on a map before you arrive - you will be close to everything, have relaxing days feeling very safe day or night (this I can't say about Dam Square or the area behind it, you can feel the under-tow of exploitation and pick-pocketing).Tip: Book popular venues, especially good local restaurants in advance (the hotel staff can do this for you) - we were fine as the end of April is still low season, but everything was pretty much booked to full capacity (not sure I would like it in the summer)OR don't worry about it and spend time in the many good bars which do just as good food. As for museums/boat trips... these were busy - not too busy, but I guess if your coming peak season then you're up against all the package tippers in their thousands.Enough said - must get on - enjoy your trip... the Estherea is remarkable for what is a BB!  
<Date>Apr 19, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Would go again Stayed here for a three night break in February 05. Booked through lastminute and got an excellent rate but sadly not an excellent room. We were right up at the top with a view of a very dull courtyard complete with rubbish bins. However, we decided that we didn't mind too much - it wasn't bad enough to demand to be moved. Room itself was small, very slightly shabby in furnishing terms, but comfortable enough. Bathroom was small but spotlessly clean, well appointed and well stocked. I think I was just disappointed that the room, whilst fine in itself, was nothing special and didn't match up to the public areas. Also the walls are paper thin and we suffered with quite a bit of noise from other rooms and the hallway.The staff were very friendly, particularly in view of the fact that I got a bug and was very, very ill on our first night - they were very solicitous and kept asking me if I was ok after that! Breakfast was excellent - plentiful and fresh.The hotel is in a fantastic location, quiet and peaceful on the canalside, with lots of bars/restaurants nearby. Try 'Broodje Bert' on the corner one block up for fantastic toasties, sandwiches etc. The Indonesian restaurant one street over is very good also.Recommended.

<Author>welshglobetrotters
<Content>The Crown Jewel of Amsterdam Imagine that you had just been invited to Amsterdam by your wealthy Aunt. She lives in a Grand and luxurious old Merchant's House alongside one of the more gentrified canals. The address, 2 minutes away from the Royal Palace at Dam Square is one of the most desireable in the City. On arrival, you step over the threshold and sink into pure wool carpets, you admire the glistening heavy chandeliers and become surrounded by luxury drapes, quality furniture and wood panelling. The gentle notes of Vivaldi diffuse effortlessly around you. Your Aunt's attentive staff are on hand to courteously assist. You are shown to your room, which also has a crystal chandelier and sumptuous furnishings. You have a large twin-sinked bathroom with an array of towels and Hydro products. All is serene, calm and feintly regal. And then you learn that everything you need to see in Amsterdam is only a few minutes walk away - that vision is the Hotel Esterea. Faultless. The reception rooms (a foyer, salon, panelled library, bar etc) are luxuriously finished in Cardinal Red, with loose-covered easy chairs, sofas and occasional tables. There is a feeling of subdued, understated oppulence - an ambience of the past. A medley of 1930's Pullman Parlour Car and a Stately home. You easily could imagine that the fellow house-guest sitting in the Library was Hercule Poirot. This is undoubtedly Amsterdam's best kept secret. THE place for the discerning traveller to stay.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Top Notch Hotel My wife and I stayed in room 410 overlooking the canal for 5 days in December 2004. The room was clean and modern with a great view. Our winter rate was only $96 euros with breakfast - very inexpensive for a hotel this nice. The lobby has been completely remodeled and looks great. The hotel is family owned and you can tell they care about it. I found the staff to be very helpful with directions, baggage, drink requests at odd hours, etc. The hotel is also within walking distance from just about everything to see in Amsterdam but the street below is fairly quiet. The breakfast was the traditional European cheese/bread/salame/cereal type thing and it was very well done. I really recommend this great hotel.
